Find out if a supply is taxable, zero-rated or exempt

The interactive tax tool (ITT) gives you personalized results based on your answers to a series of questions. The tool uses plain language to explain the most common tax situations. It is provided as a guideline only and does not replace the law.

The accuracy of your results depends on the accuracy of the information you enter. Later calculations made by the CRA may be different.

This tool does not collect or store the information you enter.

Whether or not to charge the GST/HST may depend on who the supply is made to and who makes the supply.

Use this ITT to find out if if a supply is taxable, zero-rated or exempt.

Governments
Financial institutions

  • Category of supply: Admissions (spectator)

    • Type of supply: Admission to an amateur competition or other amateur athletic event
    • Business activity: PSB - Charity
    Explanation

    Only exempt if none of the participants are professionals or are competing for cash prizes and 90% or more of the athletes or competitors are not remunerated for taking part or for appearing in advertisements for the event. Government grants and reasonable gifts, prizes and compensation for travel or other expenses are not considered remuneration.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

  • Category of supply: Admissions (spectator)

    • Type of supply: Admission to an amateur performance
    • Business activity: PSB - Charity
    Explanation

    Only exempt if 90% or more of performers are not remunerated for taking part in the performance or for appearing in advertisements for the performance. Government grants and reasonable gifts, prizes and compensation for travel or other expenses are not considered remuneration.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, s. 11 

  • Category of supply: Gambling/games of chance

    • Type of supply: Admission to an event for the purpose of gambling
    • Business activity: PSB - Charity
    Explanation

    To be exempt, the administation and operation of games must be performed 90% or more by volunteers and the place where the gambling takes place is not primarily used for gambling

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt 

    ETA: Schedule V, Part V.I, s. 6

  • Category of supply: All other supplies

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

  • Category of supply: Educational instruction

    • Type of supply: Courses leading to certificates, licences, or similar recognization by a regulatory body
    • Business activity: PSB - Govenrment or municipality
    Explanation

    The supply is taxable at 5%, 13%, or 15%, if an election has been made to make the educational services taxable. The supply is zero-rated when supplied to a non-resident (other than when supplied directly to an individual)

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part III, s. 8 Schedule VI, Part V, s. 18

  • Category of supply: Admissions (spectator)

    • Type of supply: Admission to a competitive event where professionals compete for cash prizes
    • Business activity: PSB - Hospital
    Explanation

    Admissions to competitive events are not exempt where any competitor is a professional and cash prizes are awarded. A professional golf tournament is an example.

    Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15% depending on the location

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, s. 11 

  • Category of supply: Admissions (spectator)

    • Type of supply: Admission to an amateur competition or other amateur athletic event
    • Business activity: PSB - Hospital
    Explanation

    Only exempt if none of the participants are professionals or are competing for cash prizes and 90% or more of the athletes or competitors are not remunerated for taking part or appearing in advertisements for the event. Government grants and reasonable gifts, prizes and compensation for travel or other expenses are not considered remuneration.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

  • Category of supply: Admissions (spectator)

    • Type of supply: Admission to an amateur performance
    • Business activity: PSB - Hospital
    Explanation

    Only exempt if 90% or more of performers are not remunerated for taking part in the performance or for appearing in advertisements for the performance. Government grants and reasonable gifts, prizes and compensation for travel or other expenses are not considered remuneration.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, s. 11

    • Type of supply: Health care services

    Explanation

    Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15% depending on the location

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, sections 1 and 1.1, and Schedule V, Part VI, paragraph 2(p)

    Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15% depending on the location

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, paragraph 25(c) 

  • Category of supply: All other supplies

    • Type of supply: Water
    • Business activity: PSB - Non-profit organizations (none of the other selections)
    Explanation

    Not in exempting schedule. This means that it is taxable through Division II charging provision 

    Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15% depending on the location

    ETA: S. 165(1) 

  • Category of supply: Admissions

    • Type of supply: Admission of $1 or less to a place of amusement
    • Business activity: PSB - School
    Explanation

    Admissions to a film, performance, fair, circus, rodeo, athletic contest, or museum are common examples

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, s. 9 

  • Category of supply: Admissions (spectator)

    • Type of supply: Admission to a competitive event where professionals compete for cash prizes
    • Business activity: PSB - School
    Explanation

    Admissions to competitive events are not exempt where any competitor is a professional and cash prizes are awarded. A professional golf tournament is an example.

    Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15% depending on the location

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, s. 11 

  • Category of supply: Admissions (spectator)

    • Type of supply: Admission to an amateur competition or other amateur athletic event
    • Business activity: PSB - School
    Explanation

    Only exempt if none of the participants are professionals or are competing for cash prizes and 90% or more of the athletes or competitors are not remunerated for taking part or appearing in advertisements for the event. Government grants and reasonable gifts, prizes and compensation for travel or other expenses are not considered remuneration.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

  • Category of supply: Admissions (spectator)

    • Type of supply: Admission to an amateur performance
    • Business activity: PSB - School
    Explanation

    Only exempt if 90% or more of performers are not remunerated for taking part in the performance or for appearing in advertisements for the performance. Government grants and reasonable gifts, prizes and compensation for travel or other expenses are not considered remuneration.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, s. 11 

  • Category of supply: Recreational services

    • Type of supply: Library cards and library fees
    • Business activity: PSB - School
    Explanation

    Fees for library cards and late-return fines are exempt 

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, s. 19 

  • Category of supply: Real property

    • Type of supply: Parking spaces
    • Business activity: PSB - School
    Explanation

    Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15% depending on the location

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, paragraph 25(h) 

  • Category of supply: All other supplies

    • Type of supply: Recreational camps for underpriveleged individuals and individuals with a disability
    • Business activity: PSB - School
    Explanation

    Board and lodging and recreational services at a camp or similar place provided primarily for underprivileged or disabled individuals

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt 

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, s. 13 

  • Category of supply: Educational instruction

    • Type of supply: Courses leading to certificates, licences, or similar recognization by a regulatory body
    • Business activity: PSB - School authority, university or public college
    Explanation

    The supply is taxable at 5%, 13%, or 15%, if an election has been made to make the educational services taxable. The supply is zero-rated when supplied to a non-resident (other than when supplied directly to an individual)

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part III, s. 8 Schedule VI, Part V, s. 18

  • Category of supply: Educational instruction

    • Type of supply: Credit courses that lead to diplomas and degrees
    • Business activity: PSB - School authority, university or public college
    Explanation

    Includes fees for administering exams in the same credit courses

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part III, s. 7

  • Category of supply: Educational instruction

    • Type of supply: Elementary school and secondary school instruction
    • Business activity: PSB - School authority, university or public college
    Explanation

    Applies to all courses of instruction provided primarily for elementary and secondary school students that follow a curriculum set by the province when provided by a school authority

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part III, s. 2

  • Category of supply: Educational instruction

    • Type of supply: Mandatory student fees
    • Business activity: PSB - School authority, university or public college
    Explanation

    These are fees that are mandatory to a student registered at a university, public college or school. Student council fees and athletic fees are common examples.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part III, s. 7.1

  • Category of supply: Educational instruction

    • Type of supply: Non-credit courses, offered as part of a program
    • Business activity: PSB - School authority, university or public college
    Explanation

    To be exempt, these courses must be part of a program of at least two courses. The courses cannot be related to sports, games, hobbies, or other recreational pursuits.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part III, s. 16

  • Category of supply: Educational instruction

    • Type of supply: Supplies to elementary and secondary school students during extra-curricular activities
    • Business activity: PSB - School authority, university or public college
    Explanation

    A fee to cover the cost of a class trip is a common example

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part III, s. 3

  • Category of supply: Educational instruction

    • Type of supply: Transportation service to or from school provided to elementary or secondary school students
    • Business activity: PSB - School authority, university or public college
    Explanation

    A school bus service provided to students is a common example. Does not include a service provided by one school board to another school board.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part III, s. 5

    • Type of supply: Admission to a competitive event where professionals compete for cash prizes
    • Business activity: PSB - University
    Explanation

    Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15% depending on the location

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, s. 11 

  • Category of supply: Admissions (spectator)

    • Type of supply: Admission to an amateur competition or other amateur athletic event
    • Business activity: PSB - University
    Explanation

    Only exempt if none of the participants are professionals or are competing for cash prizes and 90% or more of the athletes or competitors are not remunerated for taking part or appearing in advertisements for the event. Government grants and reasonable gifts, prizes and compensation for travel or other expenses are not considered remuneration.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

  • Category of supply: Admissions (spectator)

    • Type of supply: Admission to an amateur performance
    • Business activity: PSB - University
    Explanation

    Only exempt if 90% or more of performers are not remunerated for taking part in the performance or for appearing in advertisements for the performance. Government grants and reasonable gifts, prizes and compensation for travel or other expenses are not considered remuneration.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part VI, s. 11

  • Category of supply: Health care

    • Type of supply: Health care services - Accupuncturist
    • Business activity: Most businesses
    Requirements

    Requirements

    The acupuncture services must be rendered by a person who has one of the following:

    • Licensed or certified in the province to practise acupuncture
    • Equivalent qualifications in a province where acupuncture is not regulated
    • Licensed or certified to provide services exempted by another provision (for example, doctors, nurses, naturopathic doctors)

    Learn more: B-110 Application of the GST/HST to the Practise of Acupuncture

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, paragraph 7(l)

  • Category of supply: Health care

    • Type of supply: Health care services - Audiologist
    • Business activity: Most businesses
    Requirements

    Requirements

    Audiologist must have a Master's degree to practise in their profession and the profession is regulated in every province or territory.

    The services must be rendered to the patient that the treatment is being paid for.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, paragraph 7(g)

  • Category of supply: Health care

    • Type of supply: Health care services - Chiropractor
    • Business activity: Most businesses
    Requirements

    Requirements

    Chiropractic is regulated across Canada. Provincial colleges establish education requirements to practise in the province or territory.

    The chiropractic services must be rendered by a person who is certified or licensed to practise chiropractic in the province or territory.

    Tax status if all requirements are met: Exempt

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, paragraph 7(b)

  • Tax status: Exempt

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care service: Home care services - Bathing, feeding, assistance with dressing or medication, cleaning, laundering, meal preparation, child care, any other household or personal care service
    Important details and requirements

    Requirements

    The home case services must be:

    • Rendered to an individual who, due to age, infirmity or disability, requires assistance
    • Rendered to the individual in their home
    • Supplied or paid for by a government or municipality

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, section 13

  • Tax status: Exempt

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a dietician
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    Dieticians assess and plan nutrition care to improve health.

    Dieticians must have a Master's degree to practise in their profession and the profession is regulated in every province or territory.

    Requirements

    The services must be rendered to the patient that the treatment is being paid for.

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, section 7.1

  • Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15%

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a kinesiologist and sports therapist
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    Kinesiologists and sports therapists assess and treat sports injuries and also design programs to reduce the risk of injury.

    Kinesiology and sport's medicine are generally not regulated, although kinesiology is regulated in Ontario.

    Requirements

    A service of helping patients rehabilitate from injuries and chronic conditions is taxable (unless it is provided by a certified physiotherapist).

    ETA: Subsections 165(1) and 165(2)

  • Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15%

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a massage therapist
    Important details and requirements

    Requirements

    As of March 1, 2019, massage therapy is regulated in five provinces. Until a formal application for exemption is made by the Canadian Massage Therapy Alliance and approved by the Minister of Finance, these services are taxable.

    ETA: Subsections 165(1) and 165(2)

  • Tax status: Exempt

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a midwife
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    Midwifery is regulated in all provinces and territories, except Prince Edward Island and Yukon (both have their applications for regulation pending).

    Midwife must be certified or licensed to practise midwifery in a regulated province or territory.

    Requirements

    The midwifery services must be rendered by a person who is certified or licensed to practise midwifery in a regulated province or has equivalent qualifications in a province where midwifery is not regulated.

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, paragraph 7(k)

    ETA: Subsections 165(1) and 165(2)

  • Tax status: Exempt

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a naturopathic doctor
    Important details and requirements

    Requirements

    Service by a naturopathic doctor qualify for exemption if:

    • The supply is made after February 11, 2014
    • The practitioner has graduated from an accredited naturopathic medical program and holds a valid licence to practise as a naturopathic doctor
    • The supply is a naturopathic service rendered to an individual

    Learn more: B-109, Application of the GST/HST to the Practice of Naturopathic Doctors

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, paragraph 7(m)

  • Tax status: Exempt

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a nurse
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    Nursing involves a combination of assessing the health care needs of a patient, determining the appropriate treatment or equipment, providing supportive, preventative, therapeutic, palliative and rehabilitative treatments and administering medications.

    Nurses must have a Master's degree to practise in their profession and the profession is regulated in every province or territory.

    Requirements

    The nursing services must be rendered by a nurse to a patient within a nurse-patient relationship, regardless of the location.

    A nursing service can be rendered in a hospital, a patient's home or any other location.

    Examples

    • Registered nurse
    • Registered nursing assistant
    • Registered practical nurse
    • Registered psychiatric nurse

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, section 6

  • Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15%

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a nutritionist
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    Although there are bodies that offer certification, these are not regulated in Canada.

    Nutritionists (unlike dieticians) have varying levels of education and any person can call themselves a nutritionist with no formal education.

    Requirements

    A service of providing nutrition advice is taxable (unless it is provided by a certified dietician).

    ETA: Subsections 165(1) and 165(2)

  • Tax status: Exempt

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by an occupational therapist
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    Occupational therapists help patients recover functions of daily living.

    Occupational therapist must have a Master's degree to practise in their profession and the profession is regulated in every province or territory.

    Requirements

    The services must be rendered to the patient that the treatment is being paid for.

    Examples

    Prescribe some medications, make changes or substitutions to prescriptions, administer vaccines, order and interpret lab tests.

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, paragraph 7(i)

  • Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15%

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by an osteopath
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    Osteopathy is an alternative medicine that uses physical manipulation of muscle tissue and bones. Practitioners are referred to as Osteopathic Manual Practitioners.

    They are not Doctors of Osteopathy (DOs).Most practitioners are Osteopathic Manual Practitioners. Osteopathy is not regulated in Canada.

    Requirements

    Osteopathy services are taxable when they are provided by a person that is not a DO.

    ETA: Subsections 165(1) and 165(2)

  • Tax status: Exempt

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by an osteopathic doctor
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    Doctors of Osteopathy (DOs) have trained in the United States and hold a medical degree from a college approved by the American Osteopathic Association.

    Requirements

    The osteopathic services must be rendered by a licensed or certified DO.

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, paragraph 7(f)

  • Tax status: Exempt

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a pharmacist
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    The services that pharmacists are approved to perform have been expanding.

    Pharmacist must have a Master's degree to practise in their profession and the profession is regulated in every province or territory.

    Requirements

    Services performed by a pharmacist, other than dispensing fees, are exempt when rendered in a pharmacist-patient relationship for the promotion of the health of the patient.

    Examples

    Prescribe some medications, make changes or substitutions to prescriptions, administer vaccines, order and interpret lab tests.

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, section 7.3

  • Tax status: Exempt

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a physician or a dentist - Consultations, diagnoses, treatments, referrals, surgeries, administering vaccinations and requesting bloodwork and other diagnostic services
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    The purpose of a qualifying health care supply must be for one of the following:

    • Maintaining health
    • Preventing disease
    • Treating, relieving or remediating an injury, illness, disorder or disability
    • Assisting (other than financially) an individual in coping with an injury, illness, disorder or disability
    • Providing palliative health care

    Requirements

    To qualify, the supply:

    • Must be a consultative, diagnostic, treatment or other health care service rendered to an individual
    • Cannot be for cosmetic purposes, unless it is covered by a provincial health plan

    ETA: Schedule V, Part II, section 5

  • Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15%

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a physician or a dentist - Cosmetic services such as plastic surgery, injections, liposuction, implants, hair replacement, teeth whitening
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    Cosmetic services alter, enhance or improve the individual's appearance with no medical or reconstructive purpose.

    Requirements

    A service that is made for cosmetic purposes does not qualify for exemption unless it is for medical or reconstructive purposes or covered by a provincial health plan.

    ETA: Subsections 165(1) and 165(2)

  • Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15%

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a physician or a dentist - Independent medical exams (IME)
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    The CRA does not consider preparing an IME to be for the purpose of providing a "qualifying health care supply".

    Requirements

    The supply of an IME does not qualify for exemption unless it is incidental to a qualifying health care supply.

    Learn more: NOTICE286 Draft GST/HST Policy Statement - Qualifying Health Care Supplies and the Application of Section 1.2 of Part II of Schedule V to the Excise Tax Act to the Supply of Medical Examinations, Reports and Certificates

    ETA: Subsections 165(1) and 165(2)

  • Tax status: Taxable at 5%, 13% or 15%

    • Type of supply: Health care services
    • Type of health care services: Provided by a physician or a dentist - Management services in a medical practice
    Important details and requirements

    Details

    Management companies offer administrative services, such as payroll services, to a group of practitioners (could be any combination of practitioners and medical practitioners) practising in a medical clinic. The practitioners pay a regular fee for these services.

    Although the owner(s) or shareholder(s) of a management company may be practitioners, the management company itself cannot be a practitioner.

    Requirements

    Unless an agency relationship exists, the fees are consideration for a taxable supply.

    Learn more: P-238 Application of the GST/HST to Payments Made Between Parties Within a Medical Practice Organization

    ETA: Subsections 165(1) and 165(2)
